# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kafka Streams DSL to Processor API Migration

## Your Task

Find all Java source files in apache/kafka that implement the Kafka Streams DSL (map, filter, groupBy) and their corresponding Processor API equivalents, to support a team migrating from DSL to lower-level Processor API for custom state store management.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the migration domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kafka--0753c489, sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc, sg-evals/camel--1006f047.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/kafka--0753c489` (apache/kafka)
- `sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc` (apache/flink)
- `sg-evals/camel--1006f047` (apache/camel)

```json

```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

Perfect! I've completed a comprehensive analysis of the Apache Kafka repository (sg-evals/kafka--0753c489) and created the answer file at `/workspace/answer.json`.

## Summary of Findings

I identified **42 Java source files** implementing the Kafka Streams DSL and their corresponding Processor API equivalents:

### Core DSL Operations Found:

1. **Map Operation** - `KStreamImpl.map()` → `KStreamMap` → `ProcessorSupplier`
   - Uses `ContextualProcessor` for key-value transformations
   - Pattern: `KeyValueMapper` applies transformation, `context().forward()` sends records

2. **Filter Operation** - `KStreamImpl.filter()` → `KStreamFilter` → `FixedKeyProcessorSupplier`
   - Uses `ContextualFixedKeyProcessor` for predicate-based filtering
   - Pattern: Conditional `context().forward()` based on predicate test

3. **MapValues Operation** - `KStreamImpl.mapValues()` → `KStreamMapValues` → `FixedKeyProcessorSupplier`
   - Uses `ContextualFixedKeyProcessor` for value-only transformations
   - Pattern: Preserves key, transforms values only

4. **GroupBy Operation** - `KStreamImpl.groupBy()` → `KGroupedStreamImpl` → `GroupedStreamAggregateBuilder`
   - Creates key-changing repartition using `internalSelectKey()`
   - Chains to aggregation processors with state stores

### Key Architecture:

The analysis covers:
- **Processor API Foundation**: 10 core interfaces/classes (Processor, FixedKeyProcessor, ProcessorSupplier, ContextualProcessor, Record types, ProcessorContext)
- **KStream Operations**: 14 implementation classes for transformations and aggregations
- **KTable Operations**: 12 implementation classes for stateful table operations
- **Join Operations**: 8 classes for various join types (inner, left, right, outer)

corresponding Processor API equivalents, supporting migration from the high-level DSL to the lower-level Processor API for custom state store management.\\n\\n### Architecture Overview\\n\\nThe Kafka Streams codebase follows a clear separation between the DSL and Processor API layers:\\n\\n**Processor API Foundation** (streams/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/streams/processor/api/):\\n- `Processor.java`: Core interface for stream records with arbitrary key/value type transformations\\n- `FixedKeyProcessor.java`: Optimized processor for fixed-key streams (key doesn't change)\\n- `ProcessorSupplier.java`: Factory interface for creating Processor instances\\n- `FixedKeyProcessorSupplier.java`: Factory interface for creating FixedKeyProcessor instances\\n- `ContextualProcessor.java`: Base class extending Processor with processing context access\\n- `ContextualFixedKeyProcessor.java`: Base class extending FixedKeyProcessor with processing context access\\n- `Record.java` and `FixedKeyRecord.java`: Record wrapper interfaces\\n- `ProcessorContext.java` and `FixedKeyProcessorContext.java`: Context interfaces for state store access and record forwarding\\n\\n### Core DSL Operations\\n\\n**1. Map Operation**\\n- **DSL Entry Point**: `KStreamImpl.map()` (streams/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/streams/kstream/internals/KStreamImpl.java:283-300)\\n- **Processor Implementation**: `KStreamMap.java` implements `ProcessorSupplier<KIn, VIn, KOut, VOut>`\\n- **Inner Processor**: `KStreamMapProcessor extends ContextualProcessor<KIn, VIn, KOut, VOut>`\\n- **Key Pattern**: Transforms both key and value, changing key type (key-changing operation)\\n- **Record Flow**: `KeyValueMapper` applies transformation, `context().forward()` sends modified record\\n\\n**2. Filter Operation**\\n- **DSL Entry Point**: `KStreamImpl.filter()` (streams/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/streams/kstream/internals/KStreamImpl.java:146-172)\\n- **Processor Implementation**: `KStreamFilter.java` implements `FixedKeyProcessorSupplier<K, V, V>`\\n- **Inner Processor**: `KStreamFilterProcessor extends ContextualFixedKeyProcessor<K, V, V>`\\n- **Key Pattern**: Keeps fixed key, filters based on `Predicate<K, V>` test result\\n- **Record Flow**: Conditional forwarding using `context().forward(record)` only if predicate passes\\n\\n**3. MapValues Operation**\\n- **DSL Entry Point**: `KStreamImpl.mapValues()` (streams/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/streams/kstream/internals/KStreamImpl.java:241-280)\\n- **Processor Implementation**: `KStreamMapValues.java` implements `FixedKeyProcessorSupplier<KIn, VIn, VOut>`\\n- **Inner Processor**: `KStreamMapProcessor extends ContextualFixedKeyProcessor<KIn, VIn, VOut>`\\n- **Key Pattern**: Transforms value only, preserves key type\\n- **Record Flow**: `ValueMapperWithKey` transforms values, `context().forward()` sends modified record\\n\\n**4. key-changing operation using `internalSelectKey()` which applies `KStreamMap`\\n- **Result**: Returns `KGroupedStreamImpl<KOut, V>` for downstream aggregations\\n- **GroupedStreamAggregateBuilder**: Orchestrates repartitioning and stateful aggregation processors\\n\\n### Extended DSL Operations\\n\\n**FlatMap/FlatMapValues**:\\n- `KStreamFlatMap.java`: Implements `ProcessorSupplier` for 1-to-many key-value transformations\\n- `KStreamFlatMapValues.java`: Implements `FixedKeyProcessorSupplier` for value-only expansions\\n\\n**Stateless Operations**:\\n- `KStreamPeek.java`: Implements `FixedKeyProcessorSupplier` for side-effects without modifying records\\n- `KStreamBranch.java`: Implements `ProcessorSupplier` for conditional routing to multiple child nodes\\n- `KStreamPrint.java`: Implements `ProcessorSupplier` for debugging/printing records\\n- `ForeachProcessor.java`: Implements `Processor` for terminal side-effect operations\\n\\n**Stateful Aggregation**:\\n- `KStreamReduce.java`: Implements `KStreamAggProcessorSupplier` for reduce operations with state stores\\n- `KStreamAggregate.java`: Implements `KStreamAggProcessorSupplier` for aggregate operations with initialization\\n- `KStreamWindowAggregate.java`: Time-windowed aggregation processor\\n- `KStreamSessionWindowAggregate.java`: Session-windowed aggregation processor\\n- `KStreamSlidingWindowAggregate.java`: Sliding window aggregation processor\\n\\n### KTable DSL Operations\\n\\n**KTable.filter()**:\\n- **Processor Implementation**: `KTableFilter.java` implements store if queryable, tracks old/new values for changelog semantics\\n\\n**KTable.mapValues()**:\\n- **Processor Implementation**: `KTableMapValues.java` implements `KTableProcessorSupplier<KIn, VIn, KIn, VOut>`\\n- **Inner Processor**: `KTableMapValuesProcessor implements Processor<KIn, Change<VIn>, KIn, Change<VOut>>`\\n- **Change Records**: Operates on `Change<V>` wrappers to track old and new values for updates\\n\\n**KTable Joins**:\\n- `KTableKTableAbstractJoin.java`: Base for table-table joins (inner, left, right, outer)\\n- `KTableKTableInnerJoin.java`, `KTableKTableLeftJoin.java`, Stream-table join processor\\n- `KStreamKStreamJoin.java` and variants: Stream-stream joins with windowing\\n\\n### Implementation Patterns\\n\\n**KStream Pattern** (Key or Value Changing):\\n1. Call DSL method on `KStreamImpl` (e.g., `filter()`, `map()`)\\n2. Create `ProcessorParameters` with a `ProcessorSupplier` instance (e.g., `new KStreamFilter(predicate, false)`)\\n3. Wrap in `ProcessorGraphNode` for topology building\\n4. Return new `KStreamImpl` with graph node reference\\n5. Inner processor class extends `ContextualProcessor` or `ContextualFixedKeyProcessor`\\n6. Process method calls `context().forward()` to send records downstream\\n\\n**KTable Pattern** (Stateful):\\n1. Call DSL method on `KTableImpl` (e.g., `filter()`, `mapValues()`)\\n2. Create processor supplier implementing `KTableProcessorSupplier`\\n3. Processor receives/sends `Change<V>` records (tracking old and new values)\\n4. Materializes state store for queryability and changelog management\\n5. Returns `KGroupedStreamImpl` which chains to aggregation builders\\n3. `GroupedStreamAggregateBuilder` orchestrates repartitioning and aggregation processor deployment\\n4. Aggregation processors use state stores for incremental computations\\n\\n### Migration Implications\\n\\nFor teams migrating from DSL to Processor API for custom state store management:\\n\\n1. **Direct Replacement**: Single-operation transformations (map, filter, mapValues) can be replaced with corresponding `Processor` implementations\\n\\n2. **State Store Access**: KTable and aggregation operations require understanding of `Change<V>` records and state store lifecycle (`init()`, `close()` methods)\\n\\n3. **Record Forwarding**: DSL `context().forward()` calls must be preserved in custom processors for proper topology connectivity\\n\\n4. **Processor Suppliers**: Must implement appropriate supplier interfaces (`ProcessorSupplier`, `FixedKeyProcessorSupplier`, `KTableProcessorSupplier`)\\n\\n5. **State Management**: Stateful operations require explicit `StoreBuilder` configuration and `StoreFactory` integration\\n\\nThe clear separation between `FixedKeyProcessor` (for same-key transformations) and `Processor` (for key-changing transformations) enables compiler-level safety and performance optimizations by avoiding unnecessary key serialization overhead.\"\n}\n",

Streams codebase follows a clear separation between the DSL and Processor API layers:\\n\\n**Processor API Foundation** (streams/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/streams/processor/api/):\\n- `Processor.java`: Core interface for stream records with arbitrary key/value type transformations\\n- `FixedKeyProcessor.java`: Optimized processor for fixed-key streams (key doesn't change)\\n-
